     1→```markdown
     2→# CanvasChain Symphony – Architecture Guide  
     3→Project: `rust_blockchain_nft_expert_071` (codename *CanvasChain Symphony*)  
     4→Version: 0.8.0-alpha
     5→
     6→> “Every block is a bar; every transaction a note.” – The CanvasChain Collective
     7→
     8→---
     9→
    10→## 1. High-Level Overview
    11→CanvasChain Symphony is a constellation of **10 Rust micro-services** that collectively operate a modular blockchain-NFT platform for generative and interactive digital art.
    12→
    13→* Each “movement” (feature domain) is an **independent service** with a bounded context.  
    14→* Services communicate via **gRPC** for request/response semantics and a **NATS JetStream** event bus for pub/sub and CQRS projections.  
    15→* A custom consensus algorithm, **Proof-of-Inspiration (PoI)**, blends stake-weighted VRF elections with curator voting to periodically select a “Composer Node” that may commit a generative-art update.
    16→
    17→```
    18→┌──────────────────┐      gRPC        ┌──────────────────┐
    19→│  Wallet Service  │◀───────────────▶│  Governance Svc  │
    20→└──────────────────┘                 └──────────────────┘
    21→        ▲     ▲                               ▲
    22→        │     │  Event Bus (NATS JetStream)   │
    23→        ▼     ▼                               ▼
    24→┌──────────────────┐      Stream      ┌──────────────────┐
    25→│  Marketplace Svc │◀───────────────▶│  Minting Svc     │
    26→└──────────────────┘                 └──────────────────┘
    27→```
    28→
    29→---
    30→
    31→## 2. Micro-service Topology
    32→
    33→| Service           | Domain                           | Patterns Used                          |
    34→|-------------------|---------------------------
... (truncated)

26-assistanttool_useRead
27-usertool_resultRead
     1→# 001 – Adopt a Monorepo for Rust Microservices
     2→
     3→Status: **Approved**  
     4→Date: 2024-06-17  
     5→Tags: `repository`, `dev‐experience`, `ci/cd`, `rust`, `microservices`
     6→
     7→---
     8→
     9→## Context
    10→
    11→CanvasChain Symphony orchestrates ten specialized Rust microservices—`composition`, `minting`, `remixing`, `marketplace`, `royalty`, `wallet`, `governance`, `token-management`, `defi`, and `orchestrator`.  
    12→Early prototypes lived in independent Git repositories. While this respected bounded context, it created friction:
    13→
    14→* **Version skew**: cross-service protocol buffers, domain types and cryptographic primitives (e.g., our pluggable `CurveStrategy`) drifted, forcing tedious cherry-picks.
    15→* **Atomic evolution**: a change to a shared crate (e.g., `canvas-chain-primitives`) required synchronized releases across repos; partial updates risked network halts.
    16→* **CI💰**: each repo ran its own CI minutes; caching was duplicated and expensive.
    17→* **Dev onboarding**: cloning ten repos, wiring SSH deploy keys and remembering divergent release processes slowed contributors.
    18→
    19→Rust’s native support for [Cargo workspaces](https://doc.rust-lang.org/book/ch14-03-cargo-workspaces.html) and our need for atomic, protocol-grade versioning make a monorepo attractive.
    20→
    21→## Decision
    22→
    23→We will:
    24→
    25→1. Move all Rust microservices, shared crates (`*-primitives`, `*-proto`, etc.) and infrastructure scripts into a single repository named `canvaschain-symphony`.
    26→2. Organize code using Cargo workspaces:
    27→
    28→```
    29→canvaschain-symphony/
    30→├── Cargo.toml            # root workspace manifest
    31→├── crates/
    32→│   ├── primitive
... (truncated)

29-usertool_resultRead
     1→# ADR 002: gRPC for Service-to-Service RPC and NATS Event Bus for Asynchronous Messaging
     2→
     3→Date: 2023-11-12  
     4→Status: Accepted  
     5→Supersedes: —  
     6→Superseded by: —  
     7→Authors: Core Architecture Team (CanvasChain Symphony)
     8→
     9→---
    10→
    11→## 1. Context
    12→
    13→CanvasChain Symphony is composed of ten autonomous Rust micro-services—`composer`, `minter`, `remixer`, `market-maker`, `royalty-streamer`, etc. Each service is owned and deployed independently yet must inter-operate to deliver end-to-end user flows. Two communication patterns are required:
    14→
    15→1. **Request / Response (RPC)**  
    16→   Example: the `market-maker` service must synchronously query `token-registry` for the current royalty split before quoting a swap.
    17→
    18→2. **Publish / Subscribe (Eventing)**  
    19→   Example: the `governance` service votes on a “movement” that triggers the `composer` to mint the next artwork. Every interested service (`gallery-renderer`, `royalty-streamer`, `analytics`) must react to the same chain event without tight coupling.
    20→
    21→Key non-functional drivers:
    22→
    23→* **Performance:** high throughput, low latency, binary payloads (art layers can be large).
    24→* **Language Inter-op:** we anticipate plug-ins in Python (ML models), WASM (browser previews), and potentially Solidity-compiled bindings.
    25→* **Back-Pressure & Delivery Guarantees:** at-least-once delivery for critical NFT state transitions, but fire-and-forget for analytics streams.
    26→* **Security:** end-to-end encryption (mTLS), pluggable authN/authZ compatible with our wallet integration.
    27→
    28→---
    29→
    30→## 2. Decision
    31→
    32→1. **gRPC** will be adopted for all synchronou
... (truncated)

     1→```rust
     2→//! Node service state–machine
     3→//!
     4→//! This module implements a hierarchical, asynchronous state-machine that
     5→//! drives a single CanvasChain Symphony “conductor” (validator / full node).
     6→//!
     7→//! The public façade is [`NodeStateMachine::spawn`].  Callers provide a
     8→//! configured [`NodeContext`] plus a Tokio `mpsc::Receiver<NodeEvent>` that
     9→//! represents the node’s inbound event bus.  
    10→//!
    11→//! The machine is built around the classic State pattern.  Each state
    12→//! implements [`State`]—an async callback that receives the next event and
    13→//! returns a [`Transition`] indicating whether the machine should:
    14→//!   * stay in the same state
    15→//!   * transition to a new boxed state
    16→//!   * perform a graceful shutdown.
    17→//!
    18→//! Transitions are **total**; all event/state combinations _must_ resolve to a
    19→//! `Transition`, preventing undefined behaviour at runtime.
    20→//!
    21→//! -------------------------------------------------------------------------
    22→//! Conventions & best-practices
    23→//! -------------------------------------------------------------------------
    24→//! • Logging is performed with the `tracing` crate (structured, async-aware).  
    25→//! • All public types derive `Debug` to make tracing easier.  
    26→//! • Errors bubble up using `thiserror::Error` and are logged before causing a
    27→//!   transition into [`StateError`].  
    28→//! • No blocking I/O—everything is fully async.  
    29→//! • `#![deny(clippy::unwrap_used)]` ensures we never `.unwrap()` outside of
    30→//!   tests.  
    31→//!
    32→//! -------------------------------------------------------------------------
    33→//! Example

63-assistanttool_useRead
64-usertool_resultRead
     1→```rust
     2→//! Auction engine for the marketplace micro-service.
     3→//!
     4→//! Responsibilities
     5→//! ----------------
     6→//! 1. Create, store and track English auctions for multilayer NFTs.
     7→//! 2. Enforce bidding rules (reserve price, minimum increment, anti-sniping).
     8→//! 3. Periodically finalize ended auctions and emit events onto the service bus.
     9→//!
    10→//! The engine is designed for dependency-injection: any persistent storage that
    11→//! implements `AuctionStore` can be plugged in.  Out of the box we provide an
    12→//! in-memory implementation that is perfect for unit tests and local dev
    13→//! environments.
    14→//!
    15→//! The module is *asynchronous* and uses Tokio for non-blocking execution.
    16→//!
    17→//! # Example
    18→//! ```no_run
    19→//! # use marketplace_service::auction_engine::*;

     2→//! REST façade for CanvasChain Symphony
     3→//!
     4→//! This module exposes a small, but representative, subset of the public HTTP
     5→//! interface that external clients (CLI, mobile wallets, browsers or embedded
     6→//! installations) use to interact with the distributed CanvasChain back-end.

     9→//! the specialised micro-services via gRPC.  Whenever a request arrives, we
    10→//! perform cheap syntactic validation, enrich the tracing span with relevant
    11→//! metadata and forward the call downstream.  Results are converted back to
    12→//! idiomatic JSON before being returned to the caller.
    13→//!
    14→//! ┌──────────────────────────┐      gRPC       ┌──────────────────────────┐
    15→//! │      HTTP  Clients       ├────────────────►│  CanvasChain Services    │
    16→//! └──────────────────────────┘                 └──────────────────────────┘
    17→//!
    18→//! The gateway never touches persistent state directly, making horizontal
    19→//! scaling trivial.  All handlers are asynchronous and cancellation-safe.
    20→//!
    21→//! A note about (missing) authentication: In production we deploy the gateway
    22→//! behind an API-Key aware service mesh that injects caller identity in the
    23→//! request headers.  To keep the example self-contained, authn/authz layers
    24→//! are purposely omitted.
    25→//!
    26→//! # Conventions
    27→//! * `snake_case` query parameters
    28→//! * `camelCase` JSON bodies
    29→//! * Every successful response is wrapped in `{ "data": … }`
    30→//! * Errors conform to RFC7807 (`application/problem+json`)

    32→//! # Examples
    33→//! Minting a new multi

     1→```rust
     2→//! Persistent world-state database abstraction for CanvasChain Symphony.
     3→//!
     4→//! The `StateDb` is the canonical source of truth for chain execution.  It
     5→//! stores **accounts**, **contract byte-code** and **key–value storage** for
     6→//! every smart contract.  Each block commit generates a deterministic *state
     7→//! root* (a Blake3 Merkle accumulation of all key–value pairs) that can later
     8→//! be proven against light-client requests or off-chain indexers.
     9→//!
    10→//! Elasticity requirements of the Symphony runtime dictate that the database
    11→//! must support:
    12→//!   * atomic multi-key updates (Write-Set)
    13→//!   * cheap, read-only snapshots per block height
    14→//!   * forward-only pruning (retain the last *N* roots and fast-prune the rest)
    15→//!
    16→//! This implementation relies on `sled` for embedded, high-performance storage
    17→//! and an append-only **versioned column family** layout to avoid write
    18→//! amplification while retaining historical states.
    19→
    20→use std::{
    21→    path::{Path, PathBuf},
    22→    sync::{
    23→        atomic::{AtomicU64, Ordering},
    24→        Arc,
    25→    },
    26→};

    32→    transaction::{
    33→        ConflictableTransactionError, TransactionError, TransactionResult, Transactional,
    34→        TransactionalTree,
    35→    },

    37→};

     1→```rust
     2→//! staking_logic.rs
     3→//!
     4→//! Core staking & composer–selection logic for the CanvasChain Symphony
     5→//! staking micro-service.  This file purposefully contains no gRPC or HTTP
     6→//! plumbing;  it is meant to be embedded by the service‐layer binary and
     7→//! driven by the surrounding transport / storage adapters.
     8→//!
     9→//! Architectural notes
    10→//! -------------------
    11→//! • State is kept in-memory behind a `RwLock` and checkpointed by the
    12→//!   service into persistent storage (e.g. Postgres, RocksDB) – that part is
    13→//!   out-of-scope here.
    14→//! • Composer selection follows a simplified Proof-of-Inspiration algorithm:
    15→//!      1. Each staker submits a *VRF proof* for a given round‐seed.
    16→//!      2. The hash output is mapped to `[0, 1)`.  The staker wins if
    17→//!         output / stake_total < staker_weight.
    18→//!      3. Ties are broken deterministically by lowest hash.
    19→//! • A Strategy pattern exposes pluggable `VrfProvider`s so that collectives
    20→//!   can experiment with different curves (Ed25519, BLS, PQ, …) without
    21→//!   recompilation of the other micro-services.
    22→
    23→use std::{
    24→    collections::HashMap,
    25→    sync::Arc,

    27→};
    28→
    29→use chrono::{DateTime, Utc};

## Summary of the Technical Design Document

### 1. Impact Analysis
- Identified all 8 impacted services: `node_service`, `minting_service`, `wallet_service`, `marketplace_service`, `governance_service`, `staking_service`, `api_gateway`, and `royalty_service`
- Catalogued 5 impacted shared crates: `ccs_common`, `ccs_proto`, `ccs_db`, `ccs_consensus`, and `ccs_crypto`
- Listed 20+ critical files that require modification

### 2. Data Model Changes
- Proposed new `FractionalInfo` struct to be added to `crates/ccs_common/src/nft.rs`
- Extended `MultiLayerNft` with optional `fractional: Option<FractionalInfo>` field
- Created `FractionToken` struct for tracking ownership positions
- Added new protobuf messages in `ccs_proto` for fractionalization operations
- Designed state database extensions in `ccs_db/src/state_db.rs` for fraction storage

### 3. Component-Level Design
For each service, I detailed:
- **node_service**: New `FractionalizeNft` and `TransferFractions` transaction types in `state_machine.rs`
- **minting_service**: New `fractionalize_nft()` method in `nft_factory.rs` with gRPC endpoints
- **wallet_service**: Extended wallet metadata and new RPC methods for fraction queries
- **marketplace_service**: Modified `ListingManager` and `AuctionEngine` to support fraction trading
- **governance_service**: Weighted voting calculation based on fractional ownership
- **api_gateway**: 10+ new REST endpoints for F-NFT operations

### 4. Core User Flows
Documented two detailed sequence diagrams:
1. **Fractionalization Flow**: Owner fractionalizing an existing NFT through the full stack
2. **Purchase Flow**

High-Level Overview\nCanvasChain Symphony is a constellation of **10 Rust micro-services** that collectively operate a modular blockchain-NFT platform for generative and interactive digital art.\n\n* Each \u201cmovement\u201d (feature domain) is an **independent service** with a bounded context.  \n* Services communicate via **gRPC** for request/response semantics and a **NATS JetStream** event bus for pub/sub and CQRS projections.  \n* A custom consensus algorithm, **Proof-of-Inspiration (PoI)**, blends stake-weighted VRF elections with curator voting to periodically select a \u201cComposer Node\u201d that may commit a generative-art update.\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510      gRPC Micro-service Topology\n\n| Service           | Domain                           | Patterns Used                          |\n|-------------------|----------------------------------|----------------------------------------|\n| `wallet`          | Key management, authentication   | Strategy (crypto curves)               |\n| `governance`      | On-chain DAO voting             | State Machine, Observer                |\n| `minting`         | NFT creation / composition       | Factory, Proxy                         |\n| `remix`           | Trait evolution & layering       | State Machine, Observer                |\n| `marketplace`     | Orderbook & royalties            | Event-Driven, Proxy                    |\n| `staking`         | DeFi incentives / PoI weights    | Strategy, Event-Driven                 |\n| `discovery`       | Metadata & search index          | CQRS, Event Sourcing                   |\n| `composer`        | PoI candidate & block producer   | Strategy, State Machine                |\n| `oracle`          | Off-chain randomness / VRF       | Strategy                               |\n| `monitor`         | Telemetry & health               | Observer                               |\n\n---\n\n## 3. Inter-Service Communication\n\n### 3.1 gRPC Interface Example (Tonic)\n\n```rust\n// crates/minting/src/api.rs\nuse tonic::{Request, Response, Status};\nuse uuid::Uuid;\n\ntonic::include_proto!(\"canvaschain.minting\");\n\n#[derive(Debug, Default)]\npub struct MintingApi;\n\n#[tonic::async_trait]\nimpl minting_server::Minting for MintingApi {\n    async fn compose_nft(\n        &self,\n        req: Request<ComposeRequest>,\n    ) -> Result<Response<ComposeReply>, Status> {\n        let payload = req.into_inner();\n        let nft_id = Uuid::new_v4();\n\n        // Business logic delegates to domain layer.\n        domain::compose_nft(&payload)\n            .await\n            .map_err(|e| Status::internal(e.to_string()))?;\n\n        Ok(Response::new(ComposeReply { nft_id: nft_id.to_string() }))\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### 3.2 Event Bus Contract\n\nAll domain events are versioned and serialized with **Prost** + **Serde**.  \nSubject naming convention: `canvas.<service>.<aggregate>.<event>`.\n\n```rust\n// events/src/lib.rs\nuse chrono::{DateTime, Utc};\nuse serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};\n\npub const SCHEMA_VERSION: &str = \"v1\";\n\n#[derive(Debug, Serialize, Deserialize)]\n#[serde(tag = \"type\", content = \"payload\")]\npub enum Event {\n    NftComposed(NftComposed),\n    BidPlaced(BidPlaced),\n    GovernanceVoteCast(VoteCast),\n    // ...\n}\n\n#[derive(Debug, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct NftComposed {\n    pub nft_id: String,\n    pub composer: String,\n    pub timestamp: DateTime<Utc>,\n    pub layers: Vec<String>,\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 4. Core Design Pattern Implementations\n\n### 4.1 Factory Pattern \u2013 NFT Instrument Factory\n\n```rust\n// crates/minting/src/factory.rs\nuse super::{error::FactoryError, instruments::*};\n\npub trait InstrumentFactory: Send + Sync {\n    fn spawn(&self, spec: InstrumentSpec) -> Result<Box<dyn Instrument>, FactoryError>;\n}\n\npub struct DefaultFactory;\n\nimpl InstrumentFactory for DefaultFactory {\n    fn spawn(&self, spec: InstrumentSpec) -> Result<Box<dyn Instrument>, FactoryError> {\n        match spec.kind.as_str() {\n            \"Audio\" => Ok(Box::new(AudioInstrument::new(spec)?)),\n            \"Visual\" => Ok(Box::new(VisualInstrument::new(spec)?)),\n            \"Haptic\" => Ok(Box::new(HapticInstrument::new(spec)?)),\n            _ => Err(FactoryError::UnsupportedKind(spec.kind)),\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### 4.2 Proxy Pattern \u2013 Upgradable Smart Contract Proxy\n\n```rust\n// smart_contracts/proxy/src/lib.rs\nuse ink::env::call::{build_call, utils::ReturnType};\nuse ink::prelude::vec::Vec;\nuse ink::primitives::Clear;\n\n#[ink::contract]\nmod proxy {\n    use super::*;\n\n    #[ink(storage)]\n    pub struct Proxy {\n        implementation: AccountId,\n        admin: AccountId,\n    }\n\n    impl Proxy {\n        #[ink(constructor)]\n        pub fn new(implementation: AccountId) -> Self {\n            Self { implementation, admin: Self::env().caller() }\n        }\n\n        #[ink(message)]\n        pub fn upgrade(&mut self, new_impl: AccountId) {\n            assert_eq!(self.env().caller(), self.admin);\n            self.implementation = new_impl;\n        }\n\n        #[ink(message, payable, selector = _)]\n        pub fn fallback(&self) -> Vec<u8> {\n            let result = build_call::<ink::env::DefaultEnvironment>()\n                .call(self.implementation)\n                .transferred_value(Self::env().transferred_value())\n                .exec_input(ink::env::call::ExecutionInput::new(Self::env().selector()).push_arg(Self::env().input()))\n                .returns::<ReturnType<Vec<u8>>>()\n                .fire()\n                .expect(\"proxy call failed\");\n            result\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### 4.3 Observer Pattern \u2013 Trait Evolution Listener\n\n```rust\n// crates/remix/src/observer.rs\nuse async_nats::Subscriber;\nuse tracing::{debug, error};\n\npub async fn start_trait_observer(sub: Subscriber) -> anyhow::Result<()> {\n    while let Some(msg) = sub.next().await {\n        match serde_json::from_slice::<events::Event>(&msg.payload) {\n            Ok(events::Event::NftComposed(event)) => {\n                debug!(\"Handling NftComposed: {:?}\", event);\n                // Trigger trait evolution workflow.\n            }\n            Ok(_) => {},\n            Err(e) => error!(error = %e, \"Failed to deserialize event\"),\n        }\n    }\n    Ok(())\n}\n```\n\n### 4.4 State Machine \u2013 NFT Lifecycle\n\n```rust\n// domain/src/state_machine.rs\nuse crate::error::StateError;\nuse strum::{Display, EnumIter, EnumString};\n\n#[derive(Clone, Debug, EnumIter, EnumString, Display, PartialEq, Eq)]\npub enum NftState {\n    Draft,\n    Minted,\n    Listed,\n    Locked,\n    Transferred,\n}\n\nimpl NftState {\n    pub fn transit(self, event: &str) -> Result<NftState, StateError> {\n        use NftState::*;\n        Ok(match (self, event) {\n            (Draft, \"mint\") => Minted,\n            (Minted, \"list\") => Listed,\n            (Listed, \"lock\") => Locked,\n            (Locked, \"transfer\") => Transferred,\n            _ => return Err(StateError::InvalidTransition),\n        })\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### 4.5 Strategy Pattern \u2013 Pluggable Cryptographic Curves\n\n```rust\n// crates/crypto/src/strategy.rs\nuse ed25519_dalek as ed25519;\nuse bls_signatures::{PrivateKey as BlsPriv, Serialize as _};\nuse pqcrypto_dilithium::dilithium2;\n\npub trait SigningStrategy: Send + Sync {\n    fn sign(&self, msg: &[u8]) -> Vec<u8>;\n    fn verify(&self, msg: &[u8], sig: &[u8]) -> bool;\n}\n\npub struct Ed25519Strategy(ed25519::Keypair);\npub struct BlsStrategy(BlsPriv);\npub struct DilithiumStrategy(dilithium2::keypair::PublicKey, dilithium2::keypair::SecretKey);\n\nimpl SigningStrategy for Ed25519Strategy {\n    fn sign(&self, msg: &[u8]) -> Vec<u8> {\n        self.0.sign(msg).to_bytes().to_vec()\n    }\n    fn verify(&self, msg: &[u8], sig: &[u8]) -> bool {\n        ed25519::Signature::from_bytes(sig)\n            .and_then(|s| self.0.verify(msg, &s).map(|_| ()))\n            .is_ok()\n    }\n}\n\n// Implementations for BlsStrategy and DilithiumStrategy omitted for brevity.\n```\n\n---\n\n## 5. Consensus \u2013 Proof-of-Inspiration (PoI)\n\n```rust\n// consensus/src/poi.rs\nuse rand_core::OsRng;\nuse vrf::{openssl::CipherSuite, VRF};\n\npub struct Candidate {\n    pub node_id: String,\n    pub stake: u128,\n    pub curator_score: u64,\n}\n\npub fn elect_composer(candidates: &[Candidate], epoch: u64) -> Option<String> {\n    let total_weight: f64 = candidates\n        .iter()\n        .map(|c| (c.stake as f64) * 0.8 + (c.curator_score as f64) * 0.2)\n        .sum();\n\n    let vrf_seed = derive_epoch_seed(epoch);\n    let mut highest = None;\n    let mut highest_score = 0f64;\n\n    for c in candidates {\n        // VRF output \u2208 [0,1)\n        let vrf_out = vrf_draw(&c.node_id, vrf_seed);\n        let weighted = vrf_out * ((c.stake as f64) + 1.0).ln();\n\n        let final_score = weighted / total_weight;\n        if final_score > highest_score {\n            highest_score = final_score;\n            highest = Some(c.node_id.clone());\n        }\n    }\n    highest\n}\n\nfn vrf_draw(node_id: &str, seed: [u8; 32]) -> f64 {\n    let mut csprng = OsRng;\n    let key = CipherSuite::generate_keypair(&mut csprng);\n    let vrf = key\n        .0\n        .prove(&seed)\n        .expect(\"VRF prove failed\")\n        .hash::<sha2::Sha256>();\n    let num = u128::from_le_bytes(vrf[0..16].try_into().unwrap());\n    (num as f64) / (u128::MAX as f64)\n}\n\nfn derive_epoch_seed(epoch: u64) -> [u8; 32] {\n    use sha2::{Digest, Sha256};\n    let mut hasher = Sha256::new();\n    hasher.update(epoch.to_le_bytes());\n    hasher.finalize().into()\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 6. Error Handling & Observability\n\n* `thiserror` for domain-level error enums.  \n* `anyhow` at service boundaries for rich context.  \n* `tracing` with OpenTelemetry exporters for logs, metrics and spans.  \n* Circuit-breaker middleware on all gRPC clients using `tower::limit::ConcurrencyLimitFuture`.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Security Considerations\n\n1. Hardware-backed key storage (`yubihsm` feature flag).  \n2. Merkle-proof inclusion for off-chain metadata.  \n3. Re-entrancy guards on Ink! contracts via `non_reentrant` macro.  \n4. Formal verification pipeline (K-framework specs in `/formal_specs`).\n\n---\n\n## 8. Deployment Topology (Mermaid)\n\n```mermaid\ngraph TD\n  A[Users / DApps] -- gRPC --> B[Ingress (Envoy)]\n  B -- gRPC --> C[Wallet Svc]\n  B -- gRPC --> D[Marketplace Svc]\n  B -- gRPC --> E[Governance Svc]\n  subgraph Stateful\n    F[PostgreSQL]\n    G[Pinot Analytics]\n  end\n  C -- SQL --> F\n  D -- SQL --> F\n  E -- SQL --> F\n  D -- Stream --> G\n  subgraph Chain\n    H[(Composer Nodes)]\n  end\n  H -- PoI blocks --> D\n```\n\n---\n\n## 9. Quick-Start Commands\n\n```bash\n# Build all micro-services\ncargo make build-all\n\n# Run a local single-node testnet\ncargo run -p composer -- --dev --in-memory\n```\n\n---\n\n*Document generated: 2024-06-01*\n```",

{
  "file": {
    "content": "# 001 \u2013 Adopt a Monorepo for Rust Microservices\n\nStatus: **Approved**  \nDate: 2024-06-17  \nTags: `repository`, `dev\u2010experience`, `ci/cd`, `rust`, `microservices`\n\n---\n\n## Context\n\nCanvasChain Symphony orchestrates ten specialized Rust microservices\u2014`composition`, `minting`, `remixing`, `marketplace`, `royalty`, `wallet`, `governance`, `token-management`, `defi`, and `orchestrator`.  \nEarly prototypes lived in independent Git repositories. While this respected bounded context, it created friction:\n\n* **Version skew**: cross-service protocol buffers, domain types and cryptographic primitives (e.g., our pluggable `CurveStrategy`) drifted, forcing tedious cherry-picks.\n* **Atomic evolution**: a change to a shared crate (e.g., `canvas-chain-primitives`) required synchronized releases across repos; partial updates risked network halts.\n* **CI\ud83d\udcb0**: each repo ran its own CI minutes; caching was duplicated and expensive.\n* **Dev onboarding**: cloning ten repos, wiring SSH deploy keys and remembering divergent release processes slowed contributors.\n\nRust\u2019s native support for [Cargo workspaces](https://doc.rust-lang.org/book/ch14-03-cargo-workspaces.html) and our need for atomic, protocol-grade versioning make a monorepo attractive.\n\n## Decision\n\nWe will:\n\n1. Move all Rust microservices, shared crates (`*-primitives`, `*-proto`, etc.) and infrastructure scripts into a single repository named `canvaschain-symphony`.\n2. Organize code using Cargo workspaces:\n\n```\ncanvaschain-symphony/\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 Cargo.toml            # root workspace manifest\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 crates/\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 primitives/\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 proto/\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 curve-strategy/\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 \u2026\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 services/\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 composition/\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 minting/\n    \u2514\u2500\u2500 \u2026\n```\n\n3. Keep **one** `main` branch protected by mandatory checks. Feature work occurs in PRs with review from at least one other domain owner.\n4. Maintain **semantic versioning per crate** using `cargo-release`. A change to `canvaschain-primitives` bumps only that crate, but CI blocks merging unless all dependants still compile.\n5. Employ a top-level `Makefile.toml` (cargo-make) for common developer tasks (`make db`, `make dev-up`, etc.).\n6. Leverage GitHub Actions\u2019 shared cache: incremental build artifacts (~650 MB) are reused across microservices, cutting CI by ~55 %.\n7. Use code-owners to preserve microservice boundaries:\n\n```\n# CODEOWNERS\n/services/composition/ @art-algo @orchestrator\n/services/marketplace/ @defi-team\n/crates/primitives/ @core-protocol\n```\n\n## Consequences\n\n### Positive\n\n* **Atomic protocol upgrades** across services\u2014e.g., adding a new VRF proof to `ProofOfInspiration` requires one PR, one commit hash.\n* Unified **tooling and linting** (`cargo fmt`, `cargo clippy`, `cargo udeps`, `cargo deny`).\n* **Consistent release pipeline**: `cargo make release` builds Docker images for all changed services with version tags derived from Git metadata.\n* **Simplified local dev**: `make dev-up` spins up all services via `docker-compose`, seeded with testnet state.\n* Easier **refactoring**: `cargo fix --workspace` can propagate changes instantly.\n\n### Negative\n\n* Repo size grows quickly (projected 2 GB in 18 months). We will enforce **Git LFS** for large fixtures (e.g., generative art sample sets).\n* Potential for **cross-team merge conflicts**; mitigated by conventional commits and smaller PR scope.\n* Accidental **hidden coupling**; owners must respect microservice boundaries and avoid reaching into sibling domains.\n\n### Mitigations\n\n* **Bazel remote cache** is on our roadmap for even faster incremental builds.\n* Introduce `cargo hack` to run feature-matrix tests only on changed crates.\n* Quarterly **module sociability reviews** to detect leakage in service boundaries.\n\n---\n\n## Cargo Workspace Manifest (excerpt)\n\n```toml\n[workspace]\nmembers = [\n    \"crates/primitives\",\n    \"crates/proto\",\n    \"crates/curve-strategy\",\n    \"services/composition\",\n    \"services/minting\",\n    \"services/remixing\",\n    \"services/marketplace\",\n    \"services/royalty\",\n    \"services/wallet\",\n    \"services/governance\",\n    \"services/token-management\",\n    \"services/defi\",\n    \"services/orchestrator\",\n]\n\n[workspace.dependencies]\ntokio          = { version = \"1.37\", features = [\"rt-multi-thread\", \"macros\"] }\nprost          = \"0.12\"\ntonic          = { version = \"0.11\", features = [\"transport\"] }\ntracing        = \"0.1\"\nanyhow         = \"1\"\nthiserror      = \"1\"\nserde          = { version = \"1\", features = [\"derive\"] }\nasync-trait    = \"0.1\"\n```\n\n---\n\n## Adoption Plan\n\n1. Freeze external repos; merge them into the new `canvaschain-symphony` monorepo preserving commit history (`git subtree add`).\n2. Update CI to run workspace-aware commands (`cargo test --workspace`).\n3. Notify the community via Discord, update contributor docs, schedule \u201cdev-env day\u201d to migrate local clones.\n4. Archive old repositories as read-only.\n\n---\n\n## References\n\n* RFC-0396 \u2013 \u201cCargo Workspaces in Large Rust Projects\u201d  \n* ADR-004 \u2013 \u201cEvent Bus over gRPC\u201d  \n* Google SRE Book, Chap. 5 \u2013 \u201cMonorepos at Scale\u201d",

  "file": {
    "content": "# ADR 002: gRPC for Service-to-Service RPC and NATS Event Bus for Asynchronous Messaging\n\nDate: 2023-11-12  \nStatus: Accepted  \nSupersedes: \u2014  \nSuperseded by: \u2014  \nAuthors: Core Architecture Team (CanvasChain Symphony)\n\n---\n\n## 1. Context\n\nCanvasChain Symphony is composed of ten autonomous Rust micro-services\u2014`composer`, `minter`, `remixer`, `market-maker`, `royalty-streamer`, etc. Each service is owned and deployed independently yet must inter-operate to deliver end-to-end user flows. Two communication patterns are required:\n\n1. **Request / Response (RPC)**  \n   Example: the `market-maker` service must synchronously query `token-registry` for the current royalty split before quoting a swap.\n\n2. **Publish / Subscribe (Eventing)**  \n   Example: the `governance` service votes on a \u201cmovement\u201d that triggers the `composer` to mint the next artwork. Every interested service (`gallery-renderer`, `royalty-streamer`, `analytics`) must react to the same chain event without tight coupling.\n\nKey non-functional drivers:\n\n* **Performance:** high throughput, low latency, binary payloads (art layers can be large).\n* **Language Inter-op:** we anticipate plug-ins in Python (ML models), WASM (browser previews), and potentially Solidity-compiled bindings.\n* **Back-Pressure & Delivery Guarantees:** at-least-once delivery for critical NFT state transitions, but fire-and-forget for analytics streams.\n* **Security:** end-to-end encryption (mTLS), pluggable authN/authZ compatible with our wallet integration.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Decision\n\n1. **gRPC** will be adopted for all synchronous, intra-cluster RPC calls.  \n2. **NATS JetStream** will be adopted as the event bus for asynchronous, pub/sub communication.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Rationale\n\n### Why gRPC?\n\n* **IDL-First Development.** Protocol Buffers give us a single source of truth for message schemas in Rust, Python, TypeScript, etc.  \n* **Streaming Support.** Bidirectional streams map naturally to live trait evolution and real-time auction bidding.  \n* **Excellent Rust Ecosystem.** `tonic` provides async/await support, tower middlewares, and first-class mTLS.  \n* **Efficient Binary Encoding.** Artwork layers are sent as deltas or binary blobs; Protobuf minimizes overhead compared to JSON.  \n\n### Why NATS JetStream?\n\n* **Lightweight & Cloud-Native.** Simple single-binary, horizontal-scaling suitability for micro-k8s clusters.  \n* **Exactly-Once Semantics (Opt-In).** JetStream can persist critical events (e.g., ownership transfers) while still allowing fire-and-forget subjects for telemetry.  \n* **Observable.** Built-in tracing, ad-hocs, and integration with Grafana Promtail for distributed tracing.  \n* **Secure Subjects.** Supports leaf-nodes and account isolation, enabling multi-tenant \u201cartist pools.\u201d  \n* **Rust Client Quality.** `nats.rs` offers async, typed-structured messages and JetStream KV for on-chain state mirroring.\n\n### Alternatives Considered\n\n| Option                    | Pros                                              | Cons                                                      |\n|---------------------------|---------------------------------------------------|-----------------------------------------------------------|\n| REST/JSON over HTTP/2     | Ubiquitous, easy to debug                         | Verbose payloads, no streaming, manual schema evolution   |\n| GraphQL Federation        | Flexible querying                                 | Overkill for service-to-service calls, N + 1 traps        |\n| Apache Kafka              | Durable, massive throughput                       | Operationally heavy, zookeeper (or KRaft) complexity      |\n| RabbitMQ                  | Mature, routing patterns                          | Lower raw throughput, heavier client libs for WASM        |\n| ZeroMQ                    | Embedded-style speed                              | No central broker, discovery challenges                   |\n\ngRPC + NATS best satisfied the combined performance, ergonomics, and operational simplicity we need.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Detailed Design\n\n### 4.1 gRPC Service Definitions\n\nService contracts live in `proto/` and are versioned via Git tags. An excerpt:\n\n```protobuf\nsyntax = \"proto3\";\n\npackage canvaschain.market.v1;\n\nservice RoyaltyService {\n  // Returns the royalty split for a given NFT\n  rpc GetRoyaltyInfo(GetRoyaltyInfoRequest) returns (GetRoyaltyInfoResponse) {\n    option (google.api.http) = {\n      get: \"/v1/royalty/{token_id}\"\n    };\n  }\n}\n\nmessage GetRoyaltyInfoRequest {\n  uint64 token_id = 1;\n}\n\nmessage GetRoyaltyInfoResponse {\n  repeated Split split = 1;\n}\n\nmessage Split {\n  string recipient = 1;         // wallet address\n  uint32 share_bps   = 2;       // basis points\n}\n```\n\nRust code is generated with `prost` + `tonic_build`:\n\n```rust\n// build.rs\nfn main() -> Result<(), Box<dyn std::error::Error>> {\n    tonic_build::configure()\n        .build_server(true)\n        .build_client(true)\n        .out_dir(\"src/proto\")\n        .compile(&[\n            \"proto/canvaschain/market/v1/royalty_service.proto\",\n        ], &[\"proto\"])?;\n    Ok(())\n}\n```\n\n### 4.2 gRPC Infrastructure Patterns\n\n* **Interceptors:** Uniform wallet-signature validation (`x-canvas-sig`), request tracing (OpenTelemetry).  \n* **Resilience:** `tower::retry::Retry` with exponential backoff for transient failures.  \n* **Codegen Regeneration:** GitHub Action enforces that `cargo build --workspace` fails if `proto/` drift is detected.\n\n### 4.3 NATS JetStream Topology\n\nSubject naming convention: `domain.context.version.resource.event`  \nExample: `nft.composer.v1.artwork.minted`\n\n* **Streams:**  \n  * `core.events` \u2013 all critical state changes, storage TTL = 365 d, ack = explicit  \n  * `telemetry.metrics` \u2013 non-critical stats, storage TTL = 1 d, ack = none  \n* **Consumers:**  \n  * Durable pull consumer per microservice (`composer_core`, `gallery_renderer`, \u2026).  \n  * Ephemeral consumers for CLI tools and data scientists.\n\nRust subscription example:\n\n```rust\nlet event: MintedEvent = jetstream\n    .get_stream(\"core.events\")?\n    .create_consumer(ConsumerConfig {\n        durable_name: Some(\"gallery_renderer\".to_string()),\n        filter_subject: \"nft.composer.v1.artwork.minted\".into(),\n        deliver_policy: DeliverPolicy::All,\n        ack_policy: AckPolicy::Explicit,\n        ..Default::default()\n    })?\n    .messages()?\n    .next()\n    .await?\n    .unwrap()\n    .deserialize()?;\n```\n\n### 4.4 Transactional Outbox Pattern\n\nTo avoid dual-write hazards between the PostgreSQL command side and the event bus, each service implements the **Transactional Outbox** pattern. A reliable background task (`tokio::spawn`) pulls unsent events, publishes to NATS, and marks them dispatched. This guarantees at-least-once delivery even if the service crashes mid-transaction.\n\n![Transactional Outbox Diagram](../../design/diagrams/transactional_outbox.png)\n\n---\n\n## 5. Security Considerations\n\n* **mTLS Everywhere:** Shared SPIFFE IDs (`spiffe://canvaschain/{service}`) issued by cert-manager.  \n* **Subject ACLs:** Only the `composer` may publish on `nft.composer.*`; others read-only.  \n* **JWT Claims:** gRPC headers leverage short-lived JWTs signed by the `auth` service, propagated via NATS headers for traceability.  \n* **Replay Protection:** Nonces + timestamp fields in all state-changing Protobuf messages.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Consequences\n\n### Positive\n\n* Consistent developer experience across sync and async messaging.\n* Performance-optimized binary encoding keeps latency < 15 ms P99 inside the same AZ.\n* Pluggable structure: any service can be rewritten in another language with minimal friction.\n* Observability is unified via OpenTelemetry exporters for `tonic` and `nats.rs`.\n\n### Negative / Trade-offs\n\n* Learning curve for contributors unfamiliar with Protocol Buffers.\n* Operationally, we must maintain a NATS cluster (RAFT group) in addition to the Postgres DB.\n* Protobuf evolution requires backward-compatibility discipline to avoid breaking older miners.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Measures of Success\n\n1. End-to-end mint-to-marketplace latency \u2264 200 ms on staging.\n2. Zero lost critical events during chaos-testing (`chaos-nats` network partitions).\n3. Successful inter-op PoC of Python `remixer` plugin subscribing to `nft.*` events.\n\n---\n\n## 8. References\n\n* NATS JetStream Design: https://docs.nats.io/jetstream  \n* tonic gRPC Rust Library: https://github.com/hyperium/tonic  \n* \u201cTransactional Outbox\u201d by Pat Helland: https://microservices.io/patterns/data/transactional-outbox.html  \n* gRPC Security Best Practices: https://grpc.io/docs/guides/security/\n\n---\n\n*(END OF ADR)*",

    "content": "```rust\n//! Core NFT domain types and evolution/state-machine logic for the\n//! CanvasChain Symphony platform.\n//!\n//! This module purposefully remains *no_std*-friendly (with an opt-in\n//! `std` feature for clients that need heap allocation) so it can be\n//! reused inside on-chain WASM smart contracts as well as off-chain\n//! micro-services.\n//!\n//! Key design goals:\n//! 1. Multi-layer NFTs with independent ownership & royalty streams.\n//! 2. Fine-grained state transitions driven by user interaction,\n//!    governance votes, staking incentives and DeFi metrics.\n//! 3. Pluggable cryptography via Strategy pattern (`SignatureScheme`).\n//!\n//! NOTE: Heavy business logic such as VRF computation or signature\n//! verification lives in dedicated crates (`ccs_cryptography`, \u2026).\n#![cfg_attr(not(feature = \"std\"), no_std)]\n\nextern crate alloc;\n\nuse alloc::{\n    string::{String, ToString},\n    vec::Vec,\n    collections::BTreeMap,\n};\nuse core::{\n    fmt::{self, Display},\n    time::Duration,\n};\nuse serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};\nuse uuid::Uuid;\n\n/// New-type wrapper to avoid mixing addresses with other textual IDs.\n#[derive(Clone, Debug, PartialEq, Eq, PartialOrd, Ord, Hash, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct WalletAddress(pub String);\n\nimpl Display for WalletAddress {\n    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> fmt::Result {\n        f.write_str(&self.0)\n    }\n}\n\n/// Token amount in smallest denomination (e.g. wei, gwei, \u2026).\npub type TokenAmount = u128;\n\n/// Percentage represented in basis points (1/100th of a percent).\n/// Allowed range: 0..=10_000.\n#[derive(\n    Copy, Clone, Debug, Default, PartialEq, Eq, PartialOrd, Ord, Serialize, Deserialize,\n)]\npub struct BasisPoints(u16);\n\nimpl BasisPoints {\n    pub const MAX: u16 = 10_000;\n\n    pub fn new(bp: u16) -> Result<Self, NftError> {\n        if bp > Self::MAX {\n            Err(NftError::InvalidBasisPoints(bp))\n        } else {\n            Ok(Self(bp))\n        }\n    }\n\n    pub fn as_u16(self) -> u16 {\n        self.0\n    }\n}\n\n/// Signature strategy interface (Strategy pattern).\n/// Implementations live in the `ccs_cryptography` crate.\npub trait SignatureScheme {\n    type PublicKey;\n    type Signature;\n\n    fn verify(\n        pk: &Self::PublicKey,\n        msg: &[u8],\n        sig: &Self::Signature,\n    ) -> bool;\n}\n\n/// High-level NFT error enumeration.\n#[derive(Debug, thiserror::Error, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub enum NftError {\n    #[error(\"invalid basis points: {0}\")]\n    InvalidBasisPoints(u16),\n\n    #[error(\"layer is frozen and can\u2019t be modified: {0}\")]\n    LayerFrozen(Uuid),\n\n    #[error(\"layer not found: {0}\")]\n    UnknownLayer(Uuid),\n\n    #[error(\"ownership mismatch: expected {expected}, got {actual}\")]\n    OwnershipMismatch {\n        expected: WalletAddress,\n        actual: WalletAddress,\n    },\n\n    #[error(\"invalid state transition from {from:?} to {to:?}\")]\n    InvalidStateTransition {\n        from: LayerState,\n        to: LayerState,\n    },\n\n    #[error(\"governance vote failed: {0}\")]\n    Governance(String),\n\n    #[error(\"royalty overflow\")]\n    RoyaltyOverflow,\n}\n\n/// Layer category used for rendering, royalties etc.\n#[derive(\n    Clone, Debug, PartialEq, Eq, Hash, Serialize, Deserialize,\n)]\npub enum NftLayerKind {\n    Visual,\n    Audio,\n    Haptic,\n    Metadata,\n    Custom(String),\n}\n\n/// Finite state machine for a layer\u2019s lifecycle.\n#[derive(\n    Copy, Clone, Debug, PartialEq, Eq, Hash, Serialize, Deserialize,\n)]\npub enum LayerState {\n    Draft,\n    Active,\n    Frozen,\n    Retired,\n}\n\nimpl LayerState {\n    pub fn can_transition(self, next: LayerState) -> bool {\n        use LayerState::*;\n        matches!(\n            (self, next),\n            (Draft, Active)\n                | (Active, Frozen)\n                | (Active, Retired)\n                | (Frozen, Retired) // irreversible freeze\n        )\n    }\n}\n\n/// Event that may trigger NFT mutations.\n/// This is serialized and sent over the event bus.\n#[derive(Clone, Debug, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub enum EvolutionEvent {\n    /// A wallet interacted with the NFT (likes, remix, \u2026).\n    Interaction {\n        wallet: WalletAddress,\n        payload: alloc::vec::Vec<u8>,\n    },\n\n    /// Snapshot of staking position for DeFi incentives.\n    Staked {\n        wallet: WalletAddress,\n        amount: TokenAmount,\n        duration: Duration,\n    },\n\n    /// Governance vote outcome with yes/no ratio in basis points.\n    GovernanceResult {\n        proposal_id: Uuid,\n        approve_ratio: BasisPoints,\n    },\n}\n\n/// Single NFT layer with independent ownership & royalties.\n#[derive(Clone, Debug, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct NftLayer {\n    pub id: Uuid,\n    pub kind: NftLayerKind,\n    pub cid: String, // IPFS / Arweave content hash\n    pub state: LayerState,\n    pub owner: WalletAddress,\n    pub royalty_bp: BasisPoints,\n    pub created_at: u64,\n    pub last_updated: u64,\n}\n\nimpl NftLayer {\n    pub fn freeze(&mut self) -> Result<(), NftError> {\n        if self.state == LayerState::Frozen {\n            return Ok(());\n        }\n        if self.state.can_transition(LayerState::Frozen) {\n            self.state = LayerState::Frozen;\n            Ok(())\n        } else {\n            Err(NftError::InvalidStateTransition {\n                from: self.state,\n                to: LayerState::Frozen,\n            })\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Transfer ownership, enforcing the layer\u2019s frozen status.\n    pub fn transfer(\n        &mut self,\n        from: &WalletAddress,\n        to: WalletAddress,\n    ) -> Result<(), NftError> {\n        if &self.owner != from {\n            return Err(NftError::OwnershipMismatch {\n                expected: self.owner.clone(),\n                actual: from.clone(),\n            });\n        }\n\n        if self.state == LayerState::Frozen {\n            return Err(NftError::LayerFrozen(self.id));\n        }\n\n        self.owner = to;\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n\n/// Distribution of royalties across multiple stakeholders.\n#[derive(Clone, Debug, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct RoyaltySchedule {\n    recipients: BTreeMap<WalletAddress, BasisPoints>,\n}\n\nimpl RoyaltySchedule {\n    /// Build a new schedule. The sum of `BasisPoints` must be \u2264 10k.\n    pub fn new(\n        recipients: BTreeMap<WalletAddress, BasisPoints>,\n    ) -> Result<Self, NftError> {\n        let total: u32 = recipients\n            .values()\n            .map(|bp| bp.as_u16() as u32)\n            .sum();\n        if total > BasisPoints::MAX as u32 {\n            return Err(NftError::RoyaltyOverflow);\n        }\n        Ok(Self { recipients })\n    }\n\n    /// Resolve the royalty amount for each recipient given a sale price.\n    pub fn split(\n        &self,\n        sale_price: TokenAmount,\n    ) -> BTreeMap<WalletAddress, TokenAmount> {\n        self.recipients\n            .iter()\n            .map(|(addr, bp)| {\n                let amount = sale_price * bp.as_u16() as u128\n                    / BasisPoints::MAX as u128;\n                (addr.clone(), amount)\n            })\n            .collect()\n    }\n}\n\n/// Governance parameters per NFT.\n#[derive(Clone, Debug, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct GovernancePolicy {\n    pub quorum_bp: BasisPoints,\n    pub super_majority_bp: BasisPoints,\n    pub voting_period: Duration,\n}\n\n/// The main multi-layer NFT object.\n#[derive(Clone, Debug, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct MultiLayerNft {\n    pub id: Uuid,\n    pub name: String,\n    pub creator: WalletAddress,\n    pub layers: BTreeMap<Uuid, NftLayer>,\n    pub governance: GovernancePolicy,\n    pub royalties: RoyaltySchedule,\n}\n\nimpl MultiLayerNft {\n    /// Builder pattern entry point.\n    pub fn builder<S: Into<String>>(\n        name: S,\n        creator: WalletAddress,\n    ) -> NftBuilder {\n        NftBuilder::new(name.into(), creator)\n    }\n\n    /// Compute a deterministic content digest of all layers (Merkle root\n    /// is preferable, but we hash a concatenation for simplicity).\n    pub fn digest(&self) -> blake3::Hash {\n        let mut hasher = blake3::Hasher::new();\n        for layer in self.layers.values() {\n            hasher.update(layer.cid.as_bytes());\n        }\n        hasher.finalize()\n    }\n\n    /// Attempt to mutate the NFT based on an external event.\n    pub fn evolve(\n        &mut self,\n        event: EvolutionEvent,\n    ) -> Result<(), NftError> {\n        match event {\n            EvolutionEvent::Interaction { wallet, payload } => {\n                self.handle_interaction(wallet, payload)\n            }\n            EvolutionEvent::Staked {\n                wallet,\n                amount,\n                duration,\n            } => self.handle_stake(wallet, amount, duration),\n            EvolutionEvent::GovernanceResult {\n                proposal_id: _,\n                approve_ratio,\n            } => self.handle_governance(approve_ratio),\n        }\n    }\n\n    fn handle_interaction(\n        &mut self,\n        wallet: WalletAddress,\n        _payload: Vec<u8>,\n    ) -> Result<(), NftError> {\n        // Simple rule: first interaction grants temporary co-ownership\n        // (until frozen) of layer[0] (Visual) if not already owned.\n        if let Some(first_layer) = self.layers.values_mut().next() {\n            if first_layer.state == LayerState::Active\n                && first_layer.owner != wallet\n            {\n                first_layer.owner = wallet;\n            }\n        }\n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n    fn handle_stake(\n        &mut self,\n        _wallet: WalletAddress,\n        amount: TokenAmount,\n        duration: Duration,\n    ) -> Result<(), NftError> {\n        // Increase royalty shares proportionally to stake (toy logic).\n        let bonus_bp = (amount / 1_000_000_000_000_000_000u128) as u16; // 1 ETH == 10 bp\n        let bonus_bp = bonus_bp.min(1000); // cap at +10%\n        let adjusted = BasisPoints::new(bonus_bp)?;\n        // Add a dummy recipient (treasury) with the bonus share.\n        self.royalties.recipients.insert(\n            WalletAddress(\"canvas_treasury\".into()),\n            adjusted,\n        );\n        // Re-balance to avoid overflow (leftover goes to creator).\n        self.normalize_royalties()?;\n        // Freeze if stake duration > 30 days.\n        if duration.as_secs() >= 30 * 24 * 3600 {\n            for layer in self.layers.values_mut() {\n                layer.freeze()?;\n            }\n        }\n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n    fn handle_governance(\n        &mut self,\n        approve_ratio: BasisPoints,\n    ) -> Result<(), NftError> {\n        if approve_ratio.as_u16() >= self.governance.super_majority_bp.as_u16()\n        {\n            // Promote all `Draft` layers to `Active`.\n            for layer in self.layers.values_mut() {\n                if layer.state == LayerState::Draft {\n                    layer.state = LayerState::Active;\n                }\n            }\n            Ok(())\n        } else {\n            Err(NftError::Governance(\n                \"proposal rejected\".to_string(),\n            ))\n        }\n    }\n\n    fn normalize_royalties(&mut self) -> Result<(), NftError> {\n        let total: u32 = self\n            .royalties\n            .recipients\n            .values()\n            .map(|bp| bp.as_u16() as u32)\n            .sum();\n        if total > BasisPoints::MAX as u32 {\n            return Err(NftError::RoyaltyOverflow);\n        }\n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n    /// Transfer a specific layer to a new owner.\n    pub fn transfer_layer(\n        &mut self,\n        layer_id: Uuid,\n        from: &WalletAddress,\n        to: WalletAddress,\n    ) -> Result<(), NftError> {\n        let layer = self\n            .layers\n            .get_mut(&layer_id)\n            .ok_or(NftError::UnknownLayer(layer_id))?;\n        layer.transfer(from, to)\n    }\n}\n\n/// Fluent builder for `MultiLayerNft`.\npub struct NftBuilder {\n    id: Uuid,\n    name: String,\n    creator: WalletAddress,\n    layers: BTreeMap<Uuid, NftLayer>,\n    governance: Option<GovernancePolicy>,\n    royalties: Option<RoyaltySchedule>,\n}\n\nimpl NftBuilder {\n    fn new(name: String, creator: WalletAddress) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            id: Uuid::new_v4(),\n            name,\n            creator,\n            layers: BTreeMap::new(),\n            governance: None,\n            royalties: None,\n        }\n    }\n\n    pub fn add_layer(\n        mut self,\n        kind: NftLayerKind,\n        cid: impl Into<String>,\n        initial_state: LayerState,\n        royalty_bp: BasisPoints,\n    ) -> Self {\n        let layer = NftLayer {\n            id: Uuid::new_v4(),\n            kind,\n            cid: cid.into(),\n            state: initial_state,\n            owner: self.creator.clone(),\n            royalty_bp,\n            created_at: Self::now(),\n            last_updated: Self::now(),\n        };\n        self.layers.insert(layer.id, layer);\n        self\n    }\n\n    pub fn governance_policy(\n        mut self,\n        policy: GovernancePolicy,\n    ) -> Self {\n        self.governance = Some(policy);\n        self\n    }\n\n    pub fn royalty_schedule(\n        mut self,\n        schedule: RoyaltySchedule,\n    ) -> Self {\n        self.royalties = Some(schedule);\n        self\n    }\n\n    pub fn build(self) -> Result<MultiLayerNft, NftError> {\n        let governance = self.governance.unwrap_or(GovernancePolicy {\n            quorum_bp: BasisPoints::new(2_000)?,\n            super_majority_bp: BasisPoints::new(6_600)?,\n            voting_period: Duration::from_secs(7 * 24 * 3600),\n        });\n\n        let royalties = self.royalties.unwrap_or_else(|| {\n            let mut map = BTreeMap::new();\n            map.insert(self.creator.clone(), BasisPoints(1_000)); // 10%\n            RoyaltySchedule { recipients: map }\n        });\n\n        Ok(MultiLayerNft {\n            id: self.id,\n            name: self.name,\n            creator: self.creator,\n            layers: self.layers,\n            governance,\n            royalties,\n        })\n    }\n\n    #[inline(always)]\n    fn now() -> u64 {\n        // Use UNIX time in seconds. On chain we replace this with\n        // block-timestamp to avoid dependence on wall clock.\n        #[cfg(feature = \"std\")]\n        {\n            use std::time::{SystemTime, UNIX_EPOCH};\n            SystemTime::now()\n                .duration_since(UNIX_EPOCH)\n                .unwrap_or_default()\n                .as_secs()\n        }\n        #[cfg(not(feature = \"std\"))]\n        {\n            0\n        }\n    }\n}\n```",

This module implements a hierarchical, asynchronous state-machine that\n//! drives a single CanvasChain Symphony \u201cconductor\u201d (validator / full node).\n//!\n//! The public fa\u00e7ade is [`NodeStateMachine::spawn`].  Callers provide a\n//! configured [`NodeContext`] plus a Tokio `mpsc::Receiver<NodeEvent>` that\n//! represents the node\u2019s inbound event bus.  \n//!\n//! The machine is built around the classic State pattern.  Each state\n//! implements [`State`]\u2014an async callback that receives the next event and\n//! returns a [`Transition`] indicating whether the machine should:\n//!   * stay in the same state\n//!   * transition to a new boxed state\n//!   * perform a graceful shutdown.\n//!\n//! Transitions are **total**; all event/state combinations _must_ resolve to a\n//! `Transition`, preventing undefined behaviour at runtime.\n//!\n//! -------------------------------------------------------------------------\n//! Conventions & best-practices\n//! -------------------------------------------------------------------------\n//! \u2022 Logging is performed with the `tracing` crate (structured, async-aware).  \n//! \u2022 All public types derive `Debug` to make tracing easier.  \n//! \u2022 Errors bubble up using `thiserror::Error` and are logged before causing a\n//!   transition into [`StateError`].  \n//! \u2022 No blocking I/O\u2014everything is fully async.  \n//! \u2022 `#![deny(clippy::unwrap_used)]` ensures we never `.unwrap()` outside of\n//!   tests.  \n//!\n//! -------------------------------------------------------------------------\n//! Example\n//! -------------------------------------------------------------------------\n//! ```no_run\n//! # use tokio::sync::mpsc;\n//! # use canvas_chain_node_service::state_machine::*;\n//! # #[tokio::main]\n//! # async fn main() -> anyhow::Result<()> {\n//! let (tx, rx) = mpsc::channel(128);\n//! let ctx = NodeContext::new(Default::default(), tx.clone());\n//! let handle = NodeStateMachine::spawn(ctx, rx);\n//!\n//! // Send a dummy event\n//! tx.send(NodeEvent::Tick).await?;\n//!\n//! // Wait until the machine exits\n//! handle.await?;\n//! # Ok::<_, anyhow::Error>(())\n//! # }\n//! ```\n\n#![deny(clippy::unwrap_used)]\n\nuse std::time::Duration;\n\nuse async_trait::async_trait;\nuse tokio::{\n    select,\n    sync::mpsc,\n    task::JoinHandle,\n    time::{interval, Interval},\n};\nuse tracing::{debug, error, info, instrument};\n\nuse crate::event_bus::Publish;\nuse crate::network::types::{Block, PeerId};\nuse crate::storage::Database;\n\n// ------------------------------\n// Public facade\n// ------------------------------\n\n/// Spawn a state-machine on the Tokio runtime and return a [`JoinHandle`]\n/// representing its lifecycle.\npub struct NodeStateMachine;\n\nimpl NodeStateMachine {\n    /// Spawns the asynchronous state machine.  The function immediately returns\n    /// a Tokio [`JoinHandle`] that finishes when the machine reaches the\n    /// [`Transition::Shutdown`] transition or the provided `event_rx` closes.\n    pub fn spawn(\n        mut ctx: NodeContext,\n        mut event_rx: mpsc::Receiver<NodeEvent>,\n    ) -> JoinHandle<anyhow::Result<()>> {\n        tokio::spawn(async move {\n            let mut state: Box<dyn State> = Box::<StateBooting>::default();\n\n            // Heart-beat ticker; every state receives `Tick` events.\n            let mut ticker = interval(Duration::from_secs(5));\n\n            loop {\n                select! {\n                    maybe_evt = event_rx.recv() => {\n                        match maybe_evt {\n                            Some(evt) => {\n                                state = dispatch(&mut ctx, state, evt).await?;\n                            }\n                            None => {\n                                info!(\"event stream closed \u2013 shutting node down\");\n                                break;\n                            }\n                        }\n                    }\n\n                    _ = ticker.tick() => {\n                        state = dispatch(&mut ctx, state, NodeEvent::Tick).await?;\n                    }\n                }\n            }\n\n            info!(node_id=%ctx.config.node_id, \"node service terminated\");\n            Ok(())\n        })\n    }\n}\n\n// ------------------------------\n// Context & Events\n// ------------------------------\n\n/// Immutable configuration for a running node.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone)]\npub struct NodeConfig {\n    pub node_id: String,\n    pub network_id: String,\n    pub database_url: String,\n    pub is_validator: bool,\n}\n\nimpl Default for new(config: NodeConfig, event_tx: mpsc::Sender<NodeEvent>) -> Self {\n        let db = Database::connect(&config.database_url)\n            .expect(\"infallible for in-memory; otherwise bubble up\");\n\n        Self {\n            config,\n            db,\n            event_tx,\n            bus: Publish::default(),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// All possible events handled by the state machine.\n#[derive(Debug)]\npub enum NodeEvent {\n    /// Periodic internal heart-beat.\n    Tick,\n\n    /// New peer connected\n    PeerConnected(PeerId),\n\n    /// Network broadcast of a new block Shutdown,\n}\n\n// ------------------------------\n// State machinery\n// ------------------------------\n\n/// When a [`State`] finishes processing an event it returns a `Transition`\n/// deciding the machine\u2019s next state.\n#[derive(Debug)]\npub enum Transition {\n    /// Remain in the existing state.\n    Stay,\n    /// Replace current state with a new one.\n    Next(Box<dyn State>),\n    /// Terminate the machine.\n    Shutdown,\n}\n\n/// Common interface implemented by *every* node state.\n#[async_trait]\npub trait State: Send {\n    /// Human-readable name of the state (`&'static str` avoids allocations).\n    fn name(&self) -> &'static str;\n\n    /// Process an incoming event. Must return a valid [`Transition`].\n    async fn on_event(\n        &mut self,\n        ctx: &mut NodeContext,\n        event: NodeEvent,\n    ) -> anyhow::Result<Transition>;\n}\n\n// Wrapper that anyhow::Result<Box<dyn State>> {\n    debug!(\n        state = current.name(),\n        evt = format!(\"{:?}\", evt),\n        \"handling event\"\n    );\n\n    let transition = match current.on_event(ctx, evt).await {\n        Ok(t) => t,\n        Err(e) => {\n            error!(\"state {:?} returned error: {e:?}\", current.name());\n            return Ok(Box::new(StateError::new(e)));\n        }\n    };\n\n    let next: Box<dyn State> = match transition {\n        Transition::Stay => current,\n        Transition::Next(next_state) => next_state,\n        Transition::Shutdown => {\n            info!(\"shutdown requested by state {}\", current.name());\n            return Err(anyhow::anyhow!(\"state-machine shutdown\"));\n        }\n    };\n\n    Ok(next)\n}\n\n// ------------------------------\n// Concrete States\n// ------------------------------\n\n/// Initial boot / self-check state.\n#[derive(Default)]\nstruct info!(height = block.header.height, \"received block during sync\");\n                ctx.db.insert_block(block).await?;\n                // For brevity we assume once at tip we move to Active\n                if ctx.db.is_at_chain_tip().await? {\n                    info!(\"local chain at tip \u2013 moving to Active state\");\n                    return Ok(Transition::Next(Box::<StateActive>::default()));\n                }\n                Ok(Transition::Stay)\n            }\n            NodeEvent::Shutdown => Ok(Transition::Shutdown),\n            _ => Ok(Transition::Stay),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Fully synced, participating in consensus and answering RPCs.\n#[derive(Default)]\nstruct StateActive;\n\n#[async_trait]\nimpl State for StateActive {\n    fn name(&self) -> &'static str {\n        \"Active\"\n    }\n\n    #[instrument(skip_all)]\n    async fn on_event(\n        &mut self,\n        ctx: &mut NodeContext,\n        event: NodeEvent,\n    ) -> anyhow::Result<Transition> {\n        match event {\n            NodeEvent::ElectedComposer if ctx.config.is_validator => {\n                info!(\"\ud83c\udfb5 This node has been elected composer \u2013 creating art block\");\n                let block = compose_next_block(ctx).await?;\n                ctx.bus.publish(NodeEvent::BlockReceived(block.clone()))\n                    .await\n                    .map_err(|e| anyhow::anyhow!(\"failed to publish block: {e}\"))?;\n                ctx.db.insert_block(block).await?;\n                Ok(Transition::Stay)\n            }\n            NodeEvent::BlockReceived(block) => {\n                debug!(\n                    height = block.header.height,\n                    composer = %block.header.producer,\n                    \"applying canonical block\"\n                );\n                ctx.db.insert_block(block).await?;\n                Ok(Transition::Stay)\n            }\n            NodeEvent::Shutdown => panicking.\n#[derive(Debug)]\nstruct StateError {\n    cause: anyhow::Error,\n}\n\nimpl StateError {\n    fn new<E: Into<anyhow::Error>>(e: E) -> Self {\n        Self { cause: e.into() }\n    }\n}\n\n#[async_trait]\nimpl State for StateError {\n    fn name(&self) -> &'static str {\n        \"Error\"\n    }\n\n    async fn on_event(\n        &mut self,\n        _ctx: &mut NodeContext,\n        _event: NodeEvent,\n    ) -> anyhow::Result<Transition> {\n        error!(\"node is in error state: {:?}\", self.cause);\n        Ok(Transition::Shutdown)\n    }\n}\n\n// Factory & Strategy pattern\u2013powered NFT minting logic.\n//! Creates multilayer NFTs, signs mint payloads with a pluggable crypto\n//! backend and broadcasts events onto the internal event-bus.\n//!\n//! This file purposefully hides transport concerns (gRPC, HTTP, etc.); the\n//! factory is a pure domain component that can be wired into whatever\n//! outer-layer the micro-service exposes.\n\nuse Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct MintRequest {\n    /// Wallet address of the creator in bech32 / hex format (depends on chain).\n    pub creator_wallet: String,\n    /// An ordered list of media layers that compose the artwork.\n    pub layers: Vec<NftLayer>,\n    /// Royalty basis-points (1/100 of a percent).\n    pub royalty_bps: u16,\n    /// Arbitrary on-chain attributes (e.g. can send to the runtime.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct MintPayload {\n    pub idempotency_key: Uuid,\n    pub creator_wallet: String,\n    pub metadata_cid: String,\n    pub royalty_bps: u16,\n    pub signature: Vec<u8>,\n}\n\n/// Successful on-chain minting result.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct NftReceipt {\n    pub token_id: u64,\n    pub tx_hash: String,\n    pub signature: Vec<u8>,\n}\n\n/// ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n/// Error Handling\n/// ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\n#[derive(Error, Debug)]\npub enum FactoryError {\n    #[error(\"invalid royalty basis points: {0}\")]\n    InvalidRoyalty(u16),\n    #[error(\"mint payload validation error: {0}\")]\n    Validation(String),\n    #[error(\"crypto error: {0}\")]\n    Crypto(#[from] CryptoError),\n    #[error(\"blockchain client error: {0}\")]\n    Blockchain(#[from] BlockchainError),\n    #[error(\"event bus error: {0}\")]\n    EventBus(#[from] EventBusError),\n}\n\n#[derive(Error, Debug)]\npub {\n    #[error(\"node unreachable\")]\n    NodeUnreachable,\n    #[error(\"transaction rejected: {0}\")]\n    TransactionRejected(String),\n}\n\n#[derive(Error, Debug)]\npub enum EventBusError {\n    #[error(\"publish failed\")]\n    PublishFailed,\n}\n\n/// ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n/// Traits (Strategy / Port abstractions)\n/// ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\n/// Unified crypto-signer strategy so we can swap Ed25519, BLS, PQ, etc.\n#[async_trait]\npub trait CryptoSigner: Send + Sync {\n    /// \u2018Human\u2019 name of the algorithm (ed25519, bls12381, falcon, \u2026).\n    fn algorithm(&self) -> &'static str;\n\n    /// Public identifier derived from the secret key (hex / bech32).\n    fn public_key(&self) -> String;\n\n    /// Sign arbitrary message bytes.\n    async fn sign(&self, message: &[u8]) -> Result<Vec<u8>, CryptoError>;\n}\n\n/// Port for whatever chain client we\u2019re using (substrate, cosmos, homework-chain).\n#[async_trait]\npub trait BlockchainClient: Send + Sync {\n    async fn submit_mint(&self, payload: MintPayload) -> Result<String, BlockchainError>;\n    async fn latest_token_id(&self) -> Result<u64, BlockchainError>;\n}\n\n/// Simplistic event bus publisher (fan-out / kafka / nats / anything).\n#[async_trait]\npub trait EventPublisher: Send + Sync {\n    async fn publish<M: Serialize + Send + Sync>(&self, topic: &str, msg: &M) -> Result<(), EventBusError>;\n}\n\n/// ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n/// NFT Factory (Concrete implementation of the Factory pattern)\n/// ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\n/// Shared reference-counted pointer to immutable factory configuration.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone)]\npub struct FactoryConfig {\n    /// Maximum allowed royalty (bps). Prevents creator mistakes.\n    pub max_royalty_bps: u16,\n    /// Event bus topic for successful mints.\n    pub event_topic_success: String,\n    /// Event bus topic for failed mints.\n    pub event_topic_failure: String,\n}\n\npub struct NftFactory<S, C, E>\nwhere\n    S: CryptoSigner,\n    C: BlockchainClient,\n    E: EventPublisher,\n{\n    signer: Arc<S>,\n    chain: Arc<C>,\n    bus: Arc<E>,\n    config: Arc<FactoryConfig>,\n    // optionally keep some internal state (metrics, counters, etc.)\n    minted_counter: RwLock<u64>,\n}\n\nimpl<S, C, E> NftFactory<S, C, E>\nwhere\n    S: CryptoSigner + 'static,\n    C: BlockchainClient + 'static,\n    E: EventPublisher + 'static,\n{\n    pub fn new(signer: Arc<S>, chain: Arc<C>, bus: Arc<E>, config: FactoryConfig) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            signer,\n            chain,\n            bus,\n            config: Arc::new(config),\n            minted_counter: RwLock::new(0),\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Validate, sign, submit and broadcast the mint request.\n    #[instrument(skip_all, level = \"info\", fields(creator = %req.creator_wallet))]\n    pub async fn mint_nft(&self, req: MintRequest) -> Result<NftReceipt, FactoryError> {\n        self.validate_request(&req)?;\n\n        // ---------------------------------------------------------------------\n        // 1. Serialize metadata to JSON; in reality we would push to IPFS/Arweave\n        // and obtain a CID, we\u2019ll fake it by hashing the JSON.\n        // ---------------------------------------------------------------------\n        let metadata_json = serde_json::to_vec(&req)\n            .map_err(|e| FactoryError::Validation(format!(\"metadata serialization: {e}\")))?;\n\n        let metadata_cid = hex::encode(blake3::hash(&metadata_json).as_bytes());\n\n        // ---------------------------------------------------------------------\n        // 2. Build chain payload and sign it with the selected algorithm.\n        // ---------------------------------------------------------------------\n        let idempotency_key = Uuid::new_v4();\n        let mut payload_bytes = Vec::new();\n        payload_bytes.extend_from_slice(idempotency_key.as_bytes());\n        payload_bytes.extend_from_slice(metadata_cid.as_bytes());\n        payload_bytes.extend_from_slice(&req.royalty_bps.to_le_bytes());\n        payload_bytes.extend_from_slice(req.creator_wallet.as_bytes());\n        payload_bytes.extend_from_slice(&req.nonce.to_le_bytes());\n\n        let signature = self.signer.sign(&payload_bytes).await?;\n\n        let payload = MintPayload {\n            idempotency_key,\n            creator_wallet: req.creator_wallet.clone(),\n            metadata_cid,\n            royalty_bps: req.royalty_bps,\n            signature: signature.clone(),\n        };\n\n        // ---------------------------------------------------------------------\n        // 3. Submit mint extrinsic / transaction to the chain.\n        // ---------------------------------------------------------------------\n        let tx_hash = match self.chain.submit_mint(payload.clone()).await {\n            Ok(h) => h,\n            Err(e) => {\n                // fire & forget failure event\n                let _ = self\n                    .bus\n                    .publish(\n                        &self.config.event_topic_failure,\n                        &MintFailureEvent::from_request(&req, &format!(\"{e}\")),\n                    )\n                    .await;\n                return Err(e.into());\n            }\n        };\n\n        // ---------------------------------------------------------------------\n        // 4. Retrieve token ID (optimistic assumption we mint sequentially).\n        // ---------------------------------------------------------------------\n        let token_id = self.chain.latest_token_id().await?;\n\n        // ---------------------------------------------------------------------\n        // 5. Bump metrics & broadcast success event.\n        // ---------------------------------------------------------------------\n        {\n            let mut counter = self.minted_counter.write().await;\n            *counter += 1;\n        }\n\n        let receipt = NftReceipt {\n            token_id,\n            tx_hash: tx_hash.clone(),\n            signature,\n        };\n\n        self.bus\n            .publish(&self.config.event_topic_success, &receipt)\n            .await?;\n\n        info!(token_id, tx_hash, \"NFT minted successfully\");\n        Ok(receipt)\n    }\n\n    // -------------------\n    // internal helpers\n    // -------------------\n    fn validate_request(&self, req: &MintRequest) -> Result<(), FactoryError> {\n        if req.royalty_bps > self.config.max_royalty_bps {\n            return Err(FactoryError::InvalidRoyalty(req.royalty_bps));\n        }\n        if req.layers.is_empty() {\n            return Err(FactoryError::Validation(\"at least one layer required\".into()));\n        }\n        if req.creator_wallet.trim().is_empty() {\n            return Err(FactoryError::Validation(\"creator_wallet is empty\".into()));\n        }\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n\n/// ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n/// Event Definitions\n/// ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\n#[derive(Debug, Serialize)]\nstruct MintFailureEvent {\n    pub creator_wallet: String,\n    pub timestamp_ms: u128,\n    pub reason: String,\n}\n\nimpl MintFailureEvent {\n    fn from_request(req: &MintRequest, reason: &str) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            creator_wallet: req.creator_wallet.clone(),\n            timestamp_ms: SystemTime::now()\n                .duration_since(UNIX_EPOCH)\n                .expect(\"system time ok\")\n                .as_millis(),\n            reason: reason.to_string(),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n/// Dummy/Mock implementations behind \u2018test\u2019 feature so we can run unit tests.\n/// ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n    use std::sync::Mutex;\n\n    // --------------------\n    // Mock crypto signer\n    // --------------------\n    struct MockSigner;\n    #[async_trait]\n    impl CryptoSigner for MockSigner {\n        fn algorithm(&self) -> &'static str {\n            \"mocked-ed25519\"\n        }\n\n        fn public_key(&self) -> String {\n            \"deadbeef\".to_string()\n        }\n\n        async fn sign(&self, message: &[u8]) -> Result<Vec<u8>, CryptoError> {\n            Ok(blake3::hash(message).as_bytes().to_vec())\n        }\n    }\n\n    // --------------------\n    // Mock chain client\n    // --------------------\n    struct MockChain {\n        counter: Mutex<u64>,\n    }\n\n    #[async_trait]\n    impl BlockchainClient for MockChain {\n        async fn submit_mint(&self, _payload: MintPayload) -> Result<String, BlockchainError> {\n            let mut c = self.counter.lock().unwrap();\n            *c += 1;\n            Ok(format!(\"0x{:x}\", *c))\n        }\n\n        async fn latest_token_id(&self) -> Result<u64, BlockchainError> {\n            let c = self.counter.lock().unwrap();\n            Ok(*c)\n        }\n    }\n\n    // debug!(topic, payload, \"mock bus publish\");\n            Ok(())\n        }\n    }\n\n    #[tokio::test]\n    async fn test_mint_success() {\n        let signer = Arc::new(MockSigner);\n        let ListingStatus::Active => {\n                listing.status = ListingStatus::Reserved {\n                    buyer,\n                    reserved_at: Utc::now(),\n                };\n self.repo.get(listing_id))\n            .await\n            .map_err(|_| ListingError::Timeout)??\n            ;\n\n        if listing.owner != caller {\n            return Err(ListingError::Repository(\"Only owner can cancel\".into()));\n        }\n\n        match listing.status {\n            ListingStatus::Sold => return Err(ListingError::AlreadySold),\n            ListingStatus::Cancelled => return Err(ListingError::AlreadyCancelled),\n            _ => {}\n        }\n\n        listing.status = ListingStatus::Cancelled;\n        listing.updated_at = } => {\n                return Err(ListingError::Reserved(*reserved_buyer));\n            }\n            ListingStatus::Sold => return Err(ListingError::AlreadySold),\n            ListingStatus::Cancelled => return Err(ListingError::AlreadyCancelled),\n        }\n\n        // TODO: integrate with payment processor / smart contract to transfer funds & NFT\n\n        // When settlement succeeds:\n        listing.status = ListingStatus::Sold;\n        listing.updated_at = Utc::now();\n\n        timeout(DB_OP_TIMEOUT, self.repo.update(listing.clone()))\n            .await\n            .map_err(|_| ListingError::Timeout)??\n            ;\n\n        self.dispatch_event(MarketplaceEvent::ListingPurchased { listing_id, buyer })?;\n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n .await\n            .map_err(|_| ListingError::Timeout)?\n    }\n\n    #[instrument(skip(self))]\n    pub async fn list_active(&self) -> Result<Vec<Listing>, ListingError> {\n Create, store and track English auctions for multilayer NFTs.\n//! 2. Enforce bidding rules (reserve price, minimum increment, anti-sniping).\n//! 3. Periodically finalize ended auctions and emit events onto the service bus.\n//!\n//! The engine is designed for dependency-injection: any persistent storage that\n//! implements `AuctionStore` can be plugged in.  Out of the box we provide an\n//! in-memory implementation that is perfect for unit tests and local dev\n//! environments.\n//!\n//! The module is *asynchronous* and uses Tokio for non-blocking execution.\n//!\n//! # Example\n//! ```no_run\n//! # use marketplace_service::auction_engine::*;\n//! # #[tokio::main]\n//! # async fn main() -> anyhow::Result<()> {\n//! let engine = AuctionEngine::with_memory_store(Default::default());\n//!\n//! let auction_id = engine\n//!     .create_auction(CreateAuction {\n//!         nft_id: NftId::new(),\n//!         seller_id: UserId::new(),\n//!         reserve_price: 10_000,\n//!         duration: chrono::Duration::hours(24),\n//!     })\n//!     .await?;\n//!\n//! engine\n//!     .place_bid(auction_id, UserId::new(), 11_000)\n//!     .await?;\n//!\n//! // spawn finalize loop\n//! engine.clone().spawn_finalize_loop(tokio::time::Duration::from_secs(30));\n//! # Ok(()) }\n//! ```\n\nuse std::{\n    collections::HashMap,\n    fmt,\n    sync::Arc,\n    time::Duration as StdDuration,\n};\n\nuse async_trait::async_trait;\nuse chrono::{DateTime, Duration, Utc};\nuse                   */\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n\n/// Immutable auction parameters used for construction.\n#[derive(Debug)]\npub struct       */\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n\n#[derive(Clone, Debug, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub enum AuctionStatus {\n    Pending,\n    Active,\n  Store                                   */\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n\n/// Storage abstraction. let mut map = self.map.write().await;\n        map.insert(auction.id, auction);\n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n    async fn update(&self, auction: &Auction) -> Result<(), EngineError> {\n        let mut Err(EngineError::AuctionNotFound)\n        }\n    }\n\n    async fn get(&self, id: AuctionId) -> Result<Option<Auction>, EngineError> {\n        let map = self.map.read().await;\n
